# EC_INDEX.md — Execution Checklist Index

> **Purpose:** Tracks all Execution Checklists and their readiness status.  
> Subordinate to `docs/ai/work-packets/WORK_INDEX.md` — if status conflicts, WORK_INDEX.md wins.

> **Execution Rule:**  
> No implementation work may begin on a Work Packet unless a corresponding Execution Checklist (EC) exists in this index.

> **Status legend:**
> - `Done` — WP fully executed and validated; EC preserved for reference and regression  
> - `Draft` — EC generated and ready for execution  
> - `Blocked` — EC exists but WP dependencies are not met

> **Note:** Phase 0 ECs may be marked `Done` earlier than others due to documentation-only scope.

---

## Governing Documents

- **EC Template:** `docs/ai/execution-checklists/EC-TEMPLATE.md`
- **EC Workflow:** `docs/ai/REFERENCE/01.1-how-to-use-ecs-while-coding.md`
- **Bug Handling:** `docs/ai/REFERENCE/01.2-bug-handling-under-ec-mode.md`

All bugs must be handled through the bug handling protocol once any EC
is active. See 01.2 for the clause-driven diagnosis sequence.

> **Numbering rule for EC collisions** (locked precedent — EC-103 → EC-111 [2026-04-25],
> EC-101 → EC-114 + EC-109 → EC-115 [2026-04-27]): when a WP-keyed EC number collides
> with an existing entry in the `Registry Viewer (EC-101+ Series)` namespace, the
> WP-keyed EC retargets to the next free slot that does not shadow a known or imminent
> WP number. The viewer-series EC keeps the slot. The WP number is unchanged; only the
> EC slot moves. Add a provenance breadcrumb in the renamed checklist and a parenthetical
> retarget note in the EC_INDEX row.

| EC-094 | WP-094    | Client UI (`apps/registry-viewer/`) | **WP-094 — Viewer Hero FlatCard Key Uniqueness.** Single-file bug fix in `apps/registry-viewer/src/registry/shared.ts`. Three heroes in `wwhk` (Caiera, Miek The Unhived, Rick Jones) have two cards sharing the same `slot` because one Transforms into the other; the viewer's local `flattenSet` keyed each hero `FlatCard` on `${abbr}-hero-${hero.slug}-${card.slot}`, producing duplicate Vue `v-for` keys. Vue's keyed reconciliation treated the duplicates as a single identity and stranded one DOM node per pair, so those cards survived every filter update — the symptom on `cards.barefootbetters.com` was "these hero cards appear in every search result". Fix: change the hero-key suffix to `card.slug`; `packages/registry/src/shared.ts` deliberately untouched to preserve the engine consumer contract (`extractHeroSlug()` in `packages/game-engine/src/economy/economy.logic.ts` parses the slot suffix via last-dash). Required `// why:` comment names the three affected heroes and explains the Vue stranded-DOM consequence. No new npm deps; no test-file additions (viewer has no Vue component-test harness). | EC-194 | (no WP — ad-hoc INFRA) | Client (`apps/arena-client/src/components/play/YourVictoryPile.{vue,test.ts}`) | **Fix the `Your Victory Pile — N cards / 0 VP` stuck-zero VP rendering.** Production verification against `play.legendary-arena.com` match `yQKzaxyZykU` (2026-05-23) confirmed via Claude in Chrome: Pinia store `players[0].victoryVP = 8` (engine projection + scoring both correct), but the `[data-testid="play-your-victory-vp"]` span rendered `"0 VP"`. Forced runtime mutations to 99 / 42 / `"MARKER_777"` left the DOM unchanged while `victoryCards.length` reactivity worked normally — proving the disconnect was specific to this one prop binding. Smoking gun: the leaked attribute `victory-vp="MARKER_777"` appeared on the rendered `<section>` root (Vue `inheritAttrs: true` forwards unmatched bindings to the component root). Root cause: Vue's runtime `camelize("victory-vp") === "victoryVp"` (single cap after the hyphen), NOT `"victoryVP"`. The component declared `props: { victoryVP: { type: Number, default: 0 } }`; Vue matched the incoming kebab key against `victoryVp`, found no such prop, and silently fell back to the default `0`. `victoryCards` is unaffected because `camelize("victory-cards") === "victoryCards"` matches its declared prop name exactly. This is a documented Vue antipattern — the official style guide recommends `videoSrc` over `videoSRC` for exactly this reason. Fix: rename the YourVictoryPile prop `victoryVP` → `victoryVp` (single cap) plus the template `{{ victoryVP }}` → `{{ victoryVp }}`; update three prop-passing fixtures in `YourVictoryPile.test.ts`. The engine-layer field `UIPlayerState.victoryVP` (D-12801, mirrors `PlayerScoreBreakdown.totalVP`) STAYS as-is — read via JS property access in `PlayDesktop.vue`, `PlayMobile.vue`, `OpponentPanel.vue` (not via Vue prop binding). Parent bindings `:victory-vp="viewer.victoryVP ?? 0"` STAY as kebab — only the *resolved* camelCase target on the child side changes. No engine change, no DECISIONS entry, no `OpponentPanel.vue` change. arena-client baseline 389 / 0 fail (test count unchanged — same tests pass against the renamed prop). EC-194 follows the EC-110 / EC-166 / EC-177 / EC-178 / EC-183 / EC-192 / EC-193 ad-hoc precedent (no `WORK_INDEX.md` row; only an `EC_INDEX.md` row). See [EC-194-fix-victorypile-prop-kebab-camel-mismatch.checklist.md](EC-194-fix-victorypile-prop-kebab-camel-mismatch.checklist.md). | Done 2026-05-23 |

---

## Rules

- EC status tracks **independently** from WP completion status in `WORK_INDEX.md`
- `Draft` means the EC is generated and structurally correct
- Move to `Done` **only** when the corresponding WP is completed in `WORK_INDEX.md`
- `Blocked` applies when a WP's dependencies are known to be unmet
- This index is subordinate to `WORK_INDEX.md` — it does **not** determine execution order
- **All bug handling must follow** `docs/ai/REFERENCE/01.2-bug-handling-under-ec-mode.md` once any EC is active
